&lt;b&gt;in between there is a lot of information&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;it represents&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;a so-called hierarchical&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;hierarchical structure of the world&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For edge detection&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;that your early layers&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;output edges that are&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;more so-called coarse&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;more coarse edges&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Right, and the further up&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the more refined your edges become&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Finally you can take all of these edges&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and fuse them together&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to get one that best approximates human perception&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;such an edge&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;output result&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;also giving me a new understanding of deep learning&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;It's a very interesting, very interesting thing&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;You can think of it as a black box&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;you can think of representation learning as&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;you have data&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;right, x&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;might have some properties&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;these properties&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;maybe these good properties&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;may make it easier for you on downstream tasks&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to achieve better results&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So what you want to learn&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;from the initial data&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to this well&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;property space mapping&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;function&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;hierarchical mapping&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;to implement this&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;objective goals,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;some proxy tasks.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;what is self-supervised learning?&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;I don't have a label to directly give you,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;unlike ImageNet,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;where I have 1000 classes&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and can directly train&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;a supervised classifier&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and get a representation this way.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;In the old days,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this is what everyone was doing.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Through 1000 class labels, by the way,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;within these 1000 classes there are 200 dog&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;different breeds.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Even so,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this is why&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;ImageNet is so powerful.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Right? Even with that distribution,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;it can still let&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;our neural networks learn good representations.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;I think this is extremely impressive.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;But people also see the limitations.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Once everything is just Supervised Learning,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;there are many things you can't capture.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Because what it learns&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;— for example, we're sitting here now,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;we see these chairs,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and we now have a lot of images,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;of different chairs.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Some chairs might be quite ordinary,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;chairs in a studio like ours,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or chairs in a home,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or some designer chairs,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;right, or like an avocado chair,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;a chair shaped like an avocado.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For supervised learning,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;you need to map all of this&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to a single label,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this label is called "chair".&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So what your network has to learn,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this mapping,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is actually very, very difficult.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And it's an infinite mapping.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;It's an infinite mapping.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So it can only either memorize,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;just remember,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;recite all the chairs it's ever seen,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;through what we call spurious correlations,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;some false correlations,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;tell you it's a chair.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For example, it may not look at the chair itself&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but look at the background behind the chair,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or it thinks&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;all chairs will be next to a table,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;so it uses that to make a decision boundary&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and says,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;hey, this is a chair.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;But this is not what we want.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;What we want to achieve&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is, from this very diverse visual knowledge,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;these visual observations, to gain some kind of common sense,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;some kind of intuition.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Mm. Intuition.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Right. Or some kind of common understanding.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So this is why people initially wanted to do&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;so-called Self-Supervised Learning&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or Unsupervised Learning.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;A common misconception back then was&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;we want to do Unsupervised Learning&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;because labeling data&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is too hard and too expensive.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;We need to hire people&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to label,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;spending money and time.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;We don't want to do that.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;But that's just&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;one very small part of the problem.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The bigger issue is, in the eyes of computer vision researchers,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;everyone knew long ago&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;that only through this path&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;there's no way to give AI systems this kind of common sense.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So in 2015 and 2016,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;everyone was very, very creative.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;That period&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;was actually a quite creative era.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;People would design&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;all kinds of crazy tasks.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;These tasks —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;for example, you take an image,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;rotate it 90 degrees,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or 180 degrees,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or 270 degrees.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;You don't give these images a label,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but because you designed&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;how to rotate these images,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;right, and these images&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and their&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;rotation angles&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;can form a valid pretext task.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;You can predict how these rotated images&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;were actually rotated.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;This becomes a so-called&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;proxy task.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Similar proxy tasks also include&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;giving an image,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;converting it to grayscale,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;removing all its colors,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but then using a neural network&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to reconstruct the original colors.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Essentially, from a grayscale image,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;how do you predict&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the color of each object&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;as it should be.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And there are other similar examples,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;too many to count.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Another example, one last one:&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;let me give one more example.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The so-called Context Encoder —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;you take an image, cut out a piece in the middle,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;make it white,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and then train a neural network&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to fill in this empty part.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Fill it in.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The rationale behind all these pretext tasks is&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;that&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;humans can actually do this.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The reason humans can do this,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the reason humans know,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;hey,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;whether this image was rotated 90 or 180 degrees,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or what color the butterfly&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or house in this image should be,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;what color should it have,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;you can predict the information missing in the middle —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;all these things&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is because humans,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;based on some understanding of the physical world,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;have this common sense,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;so they can guess&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;these corrupted signals,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;these already lost signals,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;how they should be reconstructed.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The masked signals.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;But back then the problem was a hundred flowers blooming —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;all kinds of papers,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but none of them worked well.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;All the results were actually quite poor,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;all worse than ImageNet pre-training,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;by roughly 15-20 percentage points.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Percentage points.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So people were making some progress,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;moving forward step by step,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but the gap&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;uh, what ImageNet could achieve through Supervised Learning,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;learned on large-scale data,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;with labels,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the representation learned with labels,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;was still far, far better.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So, uh,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;we did something at that time,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and this was done together with Kaiming.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And this,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this architecture is called&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;called MoCo,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Momentum Contrast,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;momentum contrastive learning.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Even the Chinese name sounds interesting.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Yes, momentum contrastive learning.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Uh, I think&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;you don't need to dig into&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the specific technical details.&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;much of it is no longer important.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;it was the first to take what's called contrastive learning&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;as a framework&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and make it actually work, as a paper.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And what is contrastive learning?&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Also quite simple.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;We're now in this Representation Space,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;in this representation space,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;there are different points.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;These points may be the same object&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or completely different objects.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For example,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;I have several images of this chair,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and also some that may be tables,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or images of cats or dogs.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;These images are all different,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but in this space,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;we can measure their distances.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Or we know&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;all these different chairs —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;their images should be closer,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;their representations should be closer.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;But a chair and a cat&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;should be farther apart.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So this is the basic&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;logic of contrastive learning.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is actually not new.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;This&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;It's been done for many, many years.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;By the way, this&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;early work&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;was actually Yann who first worked with his students&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to do it.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;That's very interesting.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Of course the problem being solved&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;wasn't directly Representation Learning,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but some Metric Learning problems.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Some metric learning problems.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;But that's okay.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;This was around 2019,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;I think we gave contrastive learning&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;some new meaning.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;But this didn't come out of nowhere.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Actually before that,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the entire field was slowly moving in this direction,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;expanding.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For example, there was a paper called CPC,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and another paper called Memory Bank.&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;What does this process look like?&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;can be achieved by talking with your advisor,&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;this directional understanding.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Mm, right?&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;you must give yourself enough time and space&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to explore.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And this exploration,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this exploration phase,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;should last at least one to two months.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;What should you do during the exploration phase?&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The exploration phase —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;good question. What do you do during exploration?&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;You can't just sit there thinking.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;What you need to explore is&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;constantly hacking things,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;you really have to be like a hacker,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;playing with things,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;messing around with things.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Treat research like a game,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;like a toy to play with.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Mm, this might involve, for example,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;working through formulas,&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;finding some connections,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and perhaps more importantly, actually doing things,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;writing code.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;But when you're writing code,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;what you need to note is&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the code you write&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is not your initial starting idea&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or direction,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but an exploration process.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So the code you write&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;might simply reproduce a baseline,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;take what someone else's paper is doing&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and reproduce it.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And it might also be on the basis of this baseline&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to make some kind of extension.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And the most important thing in all this&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is to find a signal.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;it's still a bit like what you just said —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;all of this decision-making process&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is actually a quite disorderly exploration process.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;It's a&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;what we call stochastic gradient descent.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;This is a cornerstone of all machine learning,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but it equally applies to research itself&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and to our lives.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;In everyone's pursuit of their ultimate goal,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;they're all going through a stochastic&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;gradient descent process.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And I think research is the same.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For you,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the most important thing in research&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is not going from point A to point B.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For example, A is an idea,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;B is a paper,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but rather in this process,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;what kind of signal can you find?&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Your gradient,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;where exactly is your gradient?&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Kaiming's view is&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this gradient itself&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is the source of your real idea.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;When you've gone through constant exploration,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;tried many things,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;possibly unsuccessful,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;possibly successful,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;by the way, it doesn't have to be a successful experiment&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to give you this gradient.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Sometimes a failed experiment&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;gives you a larger gradient.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;That is, as long as&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the most feared thing is not knowing which direction to go.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So a good result,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;a bad result,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;are both good results.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For research,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;a surprise,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;something surprising,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;such an observation,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is always for a researcher&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;— for a researcher —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the most joyful thing.&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;he said,&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;the ideas you discover&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;are the truly your own ideas.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The idea you started with isn't your idea.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;That thing doesn't belong to you.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The idea found in exploration is your own idea.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;And the research process&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is about finding&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;your own idea.&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;or maybe you're extremely lucky,&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;So I also tell students&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;and in the end publish a paper&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;you didn't encounter any difficulties.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Why is it the worst?&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;your idea is a boring idea,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and your published paper is a boring paper.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;after many years of observation,&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;So I think this is also why&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;because&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;is actually very, very limited.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The exploration process is actually very difficult.&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;That is, this&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is actually MIT professor Bill Freeman —&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;plot,&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;So,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;This graphic has a horizontal axis&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and a vertical axis.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The horizontal axis starts from a very poor work,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;a decent work,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;a very good work,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;an exceptionally impressive work.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;This is the horizontal axis.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The vertical axis&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;is the impact on your entire career.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;The impact of this paper on your career.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So you can guess&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;what this curve actually looks like.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Right? It's not a linear curve.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;It's not that a very poor work&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;has a very bad career impact,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and the best work&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or a fairly good work&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;gives you a very good return,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;gradually increasing.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;It's not linear.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;It's saying&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;basically, a very poor work&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;actually won't hurt you much,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;nobody cares.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;No one will notice.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;A decent work —&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;no one notices either.&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;your impact&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;in any case,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;we explored the Contrastive Learning path,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and found&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;it couldn't scale up.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So we wanted to switch directions.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;So we went back&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and used a simpler approach,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;which is a kind of denoising&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;autoencoder,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this kind of autoencoder,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the Masked Autoencoder (MAE).&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;This method is even simpler.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Everyone can go read the paper,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but basically by taking some images&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and corrupting them,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;then reconstructing&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;these&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;noisy images,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;cropped images,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;or masked images,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to learn representations.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;fundamentally different from Contrastive Learning,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but its results were also very good,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;although it has very different characteristics.&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;For example, it doesn't explicitly&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;model certain environments&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;this kind of invariance&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;which causes it, when doing linear probing,&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;to perform slightly worse&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;but with untuned fine-tuning&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;these are two different ways to test representations&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;right, in that case the results would be much better&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;in any case, they have different properties&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;the representations they learn also look different&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;and these things&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;would have far-reaching consequences down the line&lt;/b&gt;
&lt;b&gt;we can talk more about this later&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;you can easily fool yourself&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;you don't have a platform&lt;/b&gt;

&lt;b&gt;at the current moment&lt;/b&gt;
